<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>

<s> rather than allow you to go on ruining her as you do; i will tell her clavering and tell all the world too that is what i swear i will do unless i can come to some terms with you and put some curb on your infernal folly <\s>

<s> you shall have six hundred a year you shall go abroad and live on that <\s>
<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>
<s> if you refuse i give you my word i'll make the real state of things known to morrow i'll swear to amory who when identified will go back to the country from whence he came and will rid the widow of you and himself together <\s>
<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>

<s> you wouldn't be so cruel to that poor boy would you pendennis <\s>

<s> it's you who are cruel to him said the old moralist <\s>
<s> why sir you'll ruin him yourself inevitably in three years <\s>
<s> yes but perhaps i won't have such dev'lish bad luck you know the luck must turn and i'll reform by gad i'll reform <\s>
<s> and if you were to split on me it would cut up my wife so you know it would most infernally <\s>
<s> to be parted from you said the old major with a sneer you know she won't live with you again <\s>

<s> live abroad or at bath or at tunbridge or at the doose and i go on here <\s>
<s> i like being here better than abroad and i like being in parliament <\s>
<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>
<s> as for your seat in parliament the major said with something of a blush on his cheek and a certain tremor which the other did not see you must part with that sir francis clavering to to me <\s>
<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>
<s> dammy does he know it too <\s>
<s> nobody knows anything out of this room pendennis answered and if you do this favour for me i hold my tongue <\s>
<s> if not i'm a man of my word and will do what i have said <\s>
<s> i say major said sir francis with a peculiarly humble smile you you couldn't get me my first quarter in advance could you like the best of fellows <\s>

<s> the little dam scoundrel i know he'll do me in the business he always does and if you could do this for me we'd see major <\s>
<s> and i think your best plan would be to go down in september to clavering to shoot and take my nephew with you and introduce him <\s>
<s> yes that will be the best time <\s>
<s> and we will try and manage about the advance <\s>

<s> will you be at home this evening or to morrow morning <\s>

<s> they've got some dev'lish good bitters in the bar <\s>
<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>

<s> as for your seat in parliament the major said with something of a blush on his cheek and a certain tremor which the other did not see you must part with that sir francis clavering to to me <\s>
<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>

<s> if not i'm a man of my word and will do what i have said <\s>

<s> the little dam scoundrel i know he'll do me in the business he always does and if you could do this for me we'd see major <\s>
<s> and i think your best plan would be to go down in september to clavering to shoot and take my nephew with you and introduce him <\s>
<s> yes that will be the best time <\s>
<s> and we will try and manage about the advance <\s>

<s> when can you get me the hundred and fifty major <\s>
<s> when shall i come and see you <\s>
<s> will you be at home this evening or to morrow morning <\s>
<s> will you have anything here <\s>
<s> they've got some dev'lish good bitters in the bar <\s>
<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>

<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>

<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>

<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>
<s> he went without any tie at all <\s>
<s> he went without dinner on fridays <\s>
<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>
<s> by gad clavering you sicken me with lies i can't help telling you so <\s>
<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>
<s> it's my belief you had rather lie than not <\s>
<s> have you come here you old old beast to tempt me to to pitch into you and and knock your old head off <\s>
<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>
<s> shouted out the old major rising to his feet and clasping his cane and looking so fiercely that the baronet's tone instantly changed towards him <\s>
<s> no no said clavering piteously i beg your pardon <\s>

<s> why have you been hunting me so <\s>
<s> do you want money out of me too <\s>
<s> by jove you know i've not got a shilling and so clavering according to his custom passed from a curse into a whimper <\s>
<s> major pendennis saw from the other's tone that clavering knew his secret was in the major's hands <\s>
<s> i've no errand from anybody or no design upon you pendennis said but an endeavour if it's not too late to save you and your family from utter ruin through the infernal recklessness of your courses <\s>
<s> i knew your secret i didn't know it when i married her upon my oath i didn't know it till the d  d scoundrel came back and told me himself and it's the misery about that which makes me so reckless pendennis indeed it is the baronet cried clasping his hands <\s>
<s> i knew your secret from the very first day when i saw amory come drunk into your dining room in grosvenor place <\s>

<s> rather than allow you to go on ruining her as you do; i will tell her clavering and tell all the world too that is what i swear i will do unless i can come to some terms with you and put some curb on your infernal folly <\s>
<s> by play debt and extravagance of all kind you've got through half your wife's fortune and that of her legitimate heirs mind her legitimate heirs <\s>
<s> here it must stop <\s>
<s> you can't live together <\s>
<s> you're not fit to live in a great house like clavering and before three years more were over would not leave a shilling to carry on <\s>

<s> you shall have six hundred a year you shall go abroad and live on that <\s>
<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>
<s> if you refuse i give you my word i'll make the real state of things known to morrow i'll swear to amory who when identified will go back to the country from whence he came and will rid the widow of you and himself together <\s>
<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>
<s> ain't i making myself pretty clearly understood <\s>
<s> you wouldn't be so cruel to that poor boy would you pendennis <\s>
<s> asked the father pleading piteously hang it think about him <\s>
<s> he's a nice boy though he's dev'lish wild i own he's dev'lish wild <\s>
<s> it's you who are cruel to him said the old moralist <\s>
<s> why sir you'll ruin him yourself inevitably in three years <\s>
<s> yes but perhaps i won't have such dev'lish bad luck you know the luck must turn and i'll reform by gad i'll reform <\s>
<s> and if you were to split on me it would cut up my wife so you know it would most infernally <\s>
<s> to be parted from you said the old major with a sneer you know she won't live with you again <\s>

<s> live abroad or at bath or at tunbridge or at the doose and i go on here <\s>
<s> i like being here better than abroad and i like being in parliament <\s>
<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>
<s> as for your seat in parliament the major said with something of a blush on his cheek and a certain tremor which the other did not see you must part with that sir francis clavering to to me <\s>
<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>

<s> nobody knows anything out of this room pendennis answered and if you do this favour for me i hold my tongue <\s>

<s> and i think your best plan would be to go down in september to clavering to shoot and take my nephew with you and introduce him <\s>

<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>

<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>

<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>

<s> the little dam scoundrel i know he'll do me in the business he always does and if you could do this for me we'd see major <\s>

<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>

<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>
<s> he went without any tie at all <\s>
<s> he went without dinner on fridays <\s>
<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>
<s> by gad clavering you sicken me with lies i can't help telling you so <\s>
<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>
<s> it's my belief you had rather lie than not <\s>
<s> have you come here you old old beast to tempt me to to pitch into you and and knock your old head off <\s>
<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>
<s> shouted out the old major rising to his feet and clasping his cane and looking so fiercely that the baronet's tone instantly changed towards him <\s>

<s> why have you been hunting me so <\s>
<s> do you want money out of me too <\s>
<s> by jove you know i've not got a shilling and so clavering according to his custom passed from a curse into a whimper <\s>

<s> i've no errand from anybody or no design upon you pendennis said but an endeavour if it's not too late to save you and your family from utter ruin through the infernal recklessness of your courses <\s>
<s> i knew your secret i didn't know it when i married her upon my oath i didn't know it till the d  d scoundrel came back and told me himself and it's the misery about that which makes me so reckless pendennis indeed it is the baronet cried clasping his hands <\s>

<s> i never forget faces <\s>

<s> rather than allow you to go on ruining her as you do; i will tell her clavering and tell all the world too that is what i swear i will do unless i can come to some terms with you and put some curb on your infernal folly <\s>
<s> by play debt and extravagance of all kind you've got through half your wife's fortune and that of her legitimate heirs mind her legitimate heirs <\s>
<s> here it must stop <\s>
<s> you can't live together <\s>
<s> you're not fit to live in a great house like clavering and before three years more were over would not leave a shilling to carry on <\s>
<s> i've settled what must be done <\s>
<s> you shall have six hundred a year you shall go abroad and live on that <\s>
<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>
<s> if you refuse i give you my word i'll make the real state of things known to morrow i'll swear to amory who when identified will go back to the country from whence he came and will rid the widow of you and himself together <\s>
<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>

<s> you wouldn't be so cruel to that poor boy would you pendennis <\s>

<s> it's you who are cruel to him said the old moralist <\s>
<s> why sir you'll ruin him yourself inevitably in three years <\s>
<s> yes but perhaps i won't have such dev'lish bad luck you know the luck must turn and i'll reform by gad i'll reform <\s>
<s> and if you were to split on me it would cut up my wife so you know it would most infernally <\s>

<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>

<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>

<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>

<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>

<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>
<s> as for your seat in parliament the major said with something of a blush on his cheek and a certain tremor which the other did not see you must part with that sir francis clavering to to me <\s>
<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>
<s> dammy does he know it too <\s>
<s> nobody knows anything out of this room pendennis answered and if you do this favour for me i hold my tongue <\s>
<s> if not i'm a man of my word and will do what i have said <\s>
<s> i say major said sir francis with a peculiarly humble smile you you couldn't get me my first quarter in advance could you like the best of fellows <\s>
<s> you can do anything with lady clavering and upon my oath i'll take up that bill of abrams <\s>
<s> the little dam scoundrel i know he'll do me in the business he always does and if you could do this for me we'd see major <\s>
<s> and i think your best plan would be to go down in september to clavering to shoot and take my nephew with you and introduce him <\s>
<s> yes that will be the best time <\s>
<s> and we will try and manage about the advance <\s>

<s> you have a mind to retire he is a clavering man and a good representative for the borough you introduce him and your people vote for him you see <\s>

<s> they've got some dev'lish good bitters in the bar <\s>
<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>

<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>
<s> he went without any tie at all <\s>
<s> he went without dinner on fridays <\s>
<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>
<s> by gad clavering you sicken me with lies i can't help telling you so <\s>
<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>
<s> it's my belief you had rather lie than not <\s>
<s> have you come here you old old beast to tempt me to to pitch into you and and knock your old head off <\s>
<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>
<s> shouted out the old major rising to his feet and clasping his cane and looking so fiercely that the baronet's tone instantly changed towards him <\s>
<s> no no said clavering piteously i beg your pardon <\s>
<s> i didn't mean to be angry or say anything unkind only you're so damned harsh to me major pendennis <\s>
<s> what is it you want of me <\s>
<s> why have you been hunting me so <\s>
<s> do you want money out of me too <\s>
<s> by jove you know i've not got a shilling and so clavering according to his custom passed from a curse into a whimper <\s>
<s> major pendennis saw from the other's tone that clavering knew his secret was in the major's hands <\s>
<s> i've no errand from anybody or no design upon you pendennis said but an endeavour if it's not too late to save you and your family from utter ruin through the infernal recklessness of your courses <\s>
<s> i knew your secret i didn't know it when i married her upon my oath i didn't know it till the d  d scoundrel came back and told me himself and it's the misery about that which makes me so reckless pendennis indeed it is the baronet cried clasping his hands <\s>
<s> i knew your secret from the very first day when i saw amory come drunk into your dining room in grosvenor place <\s>
<s> i never forget faces <\s>
<s> i remember that fellow in sydney a convict and he remembers me <\s>
<s> i know his trial the date of his marriage and of his reported death in the bush <\s>
<s> i could swear to him <\s>
<s> and i know that you are no more married to lady clavering than i am <\s>
<s> i've kept your secret well enough for i've not told a single soul that i know it not your wife not yourself till now <\s>
<s> poor lady c it would cut her up dreadfully whimpered sir francis and it wasn't my fault major you know it wasn't <\s>
<s> rather than allow you to go on ruining her as you do; i will tell her clavering and tell all the world too that is what i swear i will do unless i can come to some terms with you and put some curb on your infernal folly <\s>
<s> by play debt and extravagance of all kind you've got through half your wife's fortune and that of her legitimate heirs mind her legitimate heirs <\s>
<s> here it must stop <\s>
<s> you can't live together <\s>
<s> you're not fit to live in a great house like clavering and before three years more were over would not leave a shilling to carry on <\s>
<s> i've settled what must be done <\s>
<s> you shall have six hundred a year you shall go abroad and live on that <\s>
<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>
<s> if you refuse i give you my word i'll make the real state of things known to morrow i'll swear to amory who when identified will go back to the country from whence he came and will rid the widow of you and himself together <\s>
<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>
<s> ain't i making myself pretty clearly understood <\s>
<s> you wouldn't be so cruel to that poor boy would you pendennis <\s>
<s> asked the father pleading piteously hang it think about him <\s>
<s> he's a nice boy though he's dev'lish wild i own he's dev'lish wild <\s>
<s> it's you who are cruel to him said the old moralist <\s>
<s> why sir you'll ruin him yourself inevitably in three years <\s>
<s> yes but perhaps i won't have such dev'lish bad luck you know the luck must turn and i'll reform by gad i'll reform <\s>
<s> and if you were to split on me it would cut up my wife so you know it would most infernally <\s>
<s> to be parted from you said the old major with a sneer you know she won't live with you again <\s>

<s> live abroad or at bath or at tunbridge or at the doose and i go on here <\s>

<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>

<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>

<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>

<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>

<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>

<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>

<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>

<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>

<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>

<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>

<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>

<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>

<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>

<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>

<s> they've got some dev'lish good bitters in the bar <\s>
<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>

<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>

<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>
<s> he went without any tie at all <\s>
<s> he went without dinner on fridays <\s>
<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>
<s> by gad clavering you sicken me with lies i can't help telling you so <\s>
<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>
<s> it's my belief you had rather lie than not <\s>
<s> have you come here you old old beast to tempt me to to pitch into you and and knock your old head off <\s>
<s> said the baronet with a poisonous look of hatred at the major <\s>
<s> shouted out the old major rising to his feet and clasping his cane and looking so fiercely that the baronet's tone instantly changed towards him <\s>
<s> no no said clavering piteously i beg your pardon <\s>

<s> why have you been hunting me so <\s>
<s> do you want money out of me too <\s>
<s> by jove you know i've not got a shilling and so clavering according to his custom passed from a curse into a whimper <\s>

<s> rather than allow you to go on ruining her as you do; i will tell her clavering and tell all the world too that is what i swear i will do unless i can come to some terms with you and put some curb on your infernal folly <\s>

<s> you shall have six hundred a year you shall go abroad and live on that <\s>
<s> you must give up parliament and get on as well as you can <\s>
<s> if you refuse i give you my word i'll make the real state of things known to morrow i'll swear to amory who when identified will go back to the country from whence he came and will rid the widow of you and himself together <\s>
<s> and so that boy of yours loses at once all title to old spell's property and it goes to your wife's daughter <\s>

<s> you wouldn't be so cruel to that poor boy would you pendennis <\s>

<s> yes but perhaps i won't have such dev'lish bad luck you know the luck must turn and i'll reform by gad i'll reform <\s>

<s> live abroad or at bath or at tunbridge or at the doose and i go on here <\s>

<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>

<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>

<s> to be parted from you said the old major with a sneer you know she won't live with you again <\s>

<s> it's dev'lish convenient being in parliament <\s>
<s> there's very few seats like mine left and if i gave it to em i should not wonder the ministry would give me an island to govern or some dev'lish good thing for you know i'm a gentleman of dev'lish good family and have a handle to my name and and that sort of thing major pendennis <\s>
<s> eh don't you see <\s>
<s> don't you think they'd give me something dev'lish good if i was to play my cards well <\s>
<s> and then you know i'd save money and be kept out of the way of the confounded hells and rouge et noir and and so i'd rather not give up parliament please <\s>
<s> for at one instant to hate and defy a man at the next to weep before him and at the next to be perfectly confidential and friendly with him was not an unusual process with our versatile minded baronet <\s>
<s> as for your seat in parliament the major said with something of a blush on his cheek and a certain tremor which the other did not see you must part with that sir francis clavering to to me <\s>
<s> are you going into the house major pendennis <\s>
<s> no not i but my nephew arthur is a very clever fellow and would make a figure there and when clavering had two members his father might very likely have been one and and should like arthur to be there the major said <\s>
<s> dammy does he know it too <\s>
<s> nobody knows anything out of this room pendennis answered and if you do this favour for me i hold my tongue <\s>
<s> if not i'm a man of my word and will do what i have said <\s>
<s> i say major said sir francis with a peculiarly humble smile you you couldn't get me my first quarter in advance could you like the best of fellows <\s>
<s> you can do anything with lady clavering and upon my oath i'll take up that bill of abrams <\s>
<s> the little dam scoundrel i know he'll do me in the business he always does and if you could do this for me we'd see major <\s>
<s> and i think your best plan would be to go down in september to clavering to shoot and take my nephew with you and introduce him <\s>
<s> yes that will be the best time <\s>
<s> and we will try and manage about the advance <\s>

<s> you have a mind to retire he is a clavering man and a good representative for the borough you introduce him and your people vote for him you see <\s>
<s> when can you get me the hundred and fifty major <\s>

<s> will you be at home this evening or to morrow morning <\s>
<s> will you have anything here <\s>
<s> they've got some dev'lish good bitters in the bar <\s>
<s> i often have a glass of bitters it sets one up so <\s>
<s> the old major would take no refreshment but rose and took his leave of the baronet who walked with him to the door of the wheel of fortune and then strolled into the bar where he took a glass of gin and bitters with the landlady there and a gentleman connected with the ring who boarded at the wheel of f coming in he and sir francis clavering and the landlord talked about the fights and the news of the sporting world in general and at length mr <\s>
<s> moss abrams arrived with the proceeds of the baronet's bill from which his own handsome commission was deducted and out of the remainder sir francis stood a dinner at greenwich to his distinguished friend and passed the evening gaily at vauxhall <\s>
<s> meanwhile major pendennis calling a cab in piccadilly drove to lamb court temple where he speedily was closeted with his nephew in deep conversation <\s>
<s> after their talk they parted on very good terms and it was in consequence of that unreported conversation whereof the reader nevertheless can pretty well guess the bearing that arthur expressed himself as we have heard in the colloquy with warrington which is reported in the last chapter <\s>
<s> when a man is tempted to do a tempting thing he can find a hundred ingenious reasons for gratifying his liking and arthur thought very much that he would like to be in parliament and that he would like to distinguish himself there and that he need not care much what side he took as there was falsehood and truth on every side <\s>
<s> and on this and on other matters he thought he would compromise with his conscience and that sadduceeism was a very convenient and good humoured profession of faith <\s>
<s> phyllis and corydon on a picturesque common in the neighbourhood of tunbridge wells lady clavering had found a pretty villa whither she retired after her conjugal disputes at the end of that unlucky london season <\s>
<s> miss amory of course accompanied her mother and master clavering came home for the holidays with whom blanche's chief occupation was to fight and quarrel <\s>
<s> but this was only a home pastime and the young schoolboy was not fond of home sports <\s>
<s> he found cricket and horses and plenty of friends at tunbridge <\s>
<s> the good natured begum's house was filled with a constant society of young gentlemen of thirteen who ate and drank much too copiously of tarts and champagne who rode races on the lawn and frightened the fond mother who smoked and made themselves sick and the dining room unbearable to miss blanche <\s>
<s> she did not like the society of young gentlemen of thirteen <\s>
<s> as for that fair young creature any change as long as it was change was pleasant to her and for a week or two she would have liked poverty and a cottage and bread and cheese and for a night perhaps a dungeon and bread and water and so the move to tunbridge was by no means unwelcome to her <\s>
<s> she wandered in the woods and sketched trees and farmhouses she read french novels habitually she drove into tunbridge wells pretty often and to any play or ball or conjurer or musician who might happen to appear in the place she slept a great deal she quarrelled with mamma and frank during the morning she found the little village school and attended it and first fondled the girls and thwarted the mistress then scolded the girls and laughed at the teacher she was constant at church of course <\s>
<s> it was a pretty little church of immense antiquity a little anglo norman bijou built the day before yesterday and decorated with all sorts of painted windows carved saints heads gilt scripture texts and open pews <\s>
<s> blanche began forthwith to work a most correct high church altar cover for the church <\s>
<s> she passed for a saint with the clergyman for a while whom she quite took in and whom she coaxed and wheedled and fondled so artfully that poor mrs <\s>
<s> smirke who at first was charmed with her then bore with her then would hardly speak to her was almost mad with jealousy <\s>
<s> smirke was the wife of our old friend smirke pen's tutor and poor helen's suitor <\s>
<s> he had consoled himself for her refusal with a young lady from clapham whom his mamma provided <\s>
<s> when the latter died our friend's views became every day more and more pronounced <\s>
<s> he cut off his coat collar and let his hair grow over his back <\s>
<s> he rigorously gave up the curl which he used to sport on his forehead and the tie of his neckcloth of which he was rather proud <\s>
<s> he went without any tie at all <\s>
<s> he went without dinner on fridays <\s>
<s> he read the roman hours and intimated that he was ready to receive confessions in the vestry <\s>

<s> i've no patience with you by gad <\s>
<s> you cheat everybody yourself included <\s>
<s> i've seen a deal of the world but i never met your equal at humbugging <\s>
